      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:331px;max-width:331px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:110px;max-width:110px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:143px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_in_March_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Queen_Elizabeth_II_in_March_2015.jpg/108px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_in_March_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="108" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Queen_Elizabeth_II_in_March_2015.jpg/162px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_in_March_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Queen_Elizabeth_II_in_March_2015.jpg/216px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_in_March_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1698" data-file-height="2242"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, Queen of Australia
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:116px;max-width:116px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:143px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:David_Hurley_official_photo_(cropped,_high_resolution).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/David_Hurley_official_photo_%28cropped%2C_high_resolution%29.jpg/114px-David_Hurley_official_photo_%28cropped%2C_high_resolution%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="114" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/David_Hurley_official_photo_%28cropped%2C_high_resolution%29.jpg/171px-David_Hurley_official_photo_%28cropped%2C_high_resolution%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/David_Hurley_official_photo_%28cropped%2C_high_resolution%29.jpg/228px-David_Hurley_official_photo_%28cropped%2C_high_resolution%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1188" data-file-height="1485"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/David_Hurley" title="David Hurley">David Hurley</a>, Governor-General of Australia
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:99px;max-width:99px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:143px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Scott_Morrison_2014_crop.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Scott_Morrison_2014_crop.jpg/97px-Scott_Morrison_2014_crop.jpg" decoding="async" width="97" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Scott_Morrison_2014_crop.jpg/146px-Scott_Morrison_2014_crop.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Scott_Morrison_2014_crop.jpg/194px-Scott_Morrison_2014_crop.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1856" data-file-height="2728"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Scott_Morrison" title="Scott Morrison">Scott Morrison</a>, Prime Minister of Australia
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia is a <a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[189]</a></sup> The country has maintained a stable <a href="/wiki/Liberal_democracy" title="Liberal democracy">liberal democratic</a> political system under its <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Australia" title="Constitution of Australia">constitution</a>, which is <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_constitutions" title="List of national constitutions">one of the world's oldest</a>, since <a href="/wiki/Federation_of_Australia" title="Federation of Australia">Federation</a> in 1901. It is also one of the world's oldest <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federations</a>, in which power is divided between the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Australia">federal</a> and <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">state and territorial</a> governments. The Australian system of government combines elements derived from the political systems of the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">United Kingdom</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Fusion_of_powers" title="Fusion of powers">fused executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> and strong <a href="/wiki/Party_discipline" title="Party discipline">party discipline</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Government">United States</a> (<a href="/wiki/Federalism" title="Federalism">federalism</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Written_constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Written constitution">written constitution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">strong bicameralism</a> with an elected upper house), along with distinctive indigenous features.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[191]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The federal government is <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_powers_in_Australia" title="Separation of powers in Australia">separated</a> into three branches:<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[192]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>Legislature: the bicameral <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Australia" title="Parliament of Australia">Parliament</a>, comprising the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Australia" title="Monarchy of Australia">monarch</a> (represented by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">governor-general</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Senate" title="Australian Senate">Senate</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_House_of_Representatives" title="Australian House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>;</li>
      </ul> 
      <ul>
       <li>Executive: the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Executive_Council_(Australia)" title="Federal Executive Council (Australia)">Federal Executive Council</a>, which in practice gives legal effect to the decisions of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Australia" title="Cabinet of Australia">cabinet</a>, comprising the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">prime minister</a> and other ministers of state appointed by the governor-general on the advice of Parliament;<sup id="cite_ref-CIAfactbook_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAfactbook-200">[193]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <ul>
       <li>Judiciary: the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Australia" title="High Court of Australia">High Court of Australia</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Australian_court_hierarchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian court hierarchy">federal courts</a>, whose judges are appointed by the governor-general on advice of Parliament</li>
      </ul> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> reigns as <a href="/wiki/Queen_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen of Australia">Queen of Australia</a> and is represented in Australia by the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">governor-general</a> at the federal level and by the <a href="/wiki/Governors_of_the_Australian_states" title="Governors of the Australian states">governors</a> at the state level, who by convention act on the advice of her ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-Davison_pp287–8_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davison_pp287–8-201">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[195]</a></sup> Thus, in practice the governor-general acts as a legal figurehead for the actions of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">prime minister</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Executive_Council_(Australia)" title="Federal Executive Council (Australia)">Federal Executive Council</a>. The governor-general does have extraordinary <a href="/wiki/Reserve_power" title="Reserve power">reserve powers</a> which may be exercised outside the prime minister's request in rare and limited circumstances, the most notable exercise of which was the dismissal of the Whitlam Government in the <a href="/wiki/1975_Australian_constitutional_crisis" title="1975 Australian constitutional crisis">constitutional crisis of 1975</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[196]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_House_at_dusk,_Canberra_ACT.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A large white and cream coloured building with grass on its roof. The building is topped with a large flagpole." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg/220px-Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg/330px-Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg/440px-Parliament_House_at_dusk%2C_Canberra_ACT.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5505" data-file-height="3670"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parliament_House_at_dusk,_Canberra_ACT.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Parliament_House,_Canberra" title="Parliament House, Canberra">Parliament House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the Senate (the upper house), there are 76 senators: twelve each from the states and two each from the mainland territories (the Australian Capital Territory and the Northern Territory).<sup id="cite_ref-sen_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sen-204">[197]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Australian_House_of_Representatives" title="Australian House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> (the lower house) has 151 members elected from single-member <a href="/wiki/Divisions_of_the_Australian_House_of_Representatives" title="Divisions of the Australian House of Representatives">electoral divisions</a>, commonly known as "electorates" or "seats", allocated to states on the basis of population,<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[198]</a></sup> with each original state guaranteed a minimum of five seats.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[199]</a></sup> Elections for both chambers are normally held every three years simultaneously; senators have overlapping six-year terms except for those from the territories, whose terms are not fixed but are tied to the electoral cycle for the lower house; thus only 40 of the 76 places in the Senate are put to each election unless the cycle is interrupted by a <a href="/wiki/Double_dissolution" title="Double dissolution">double dissolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sen_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sen-204">[197]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia's <a href="/wiki/Electoral_system_of_Australia" title="Electoral system of Australia">electoral system</a> uses <a href="/wiki/Instant-runoff_voting" title="Instant-runoff voting">preferential voting</a> for all lower house elections with the exception of Tasmania and the ACT which, along with the Senate and most state upper houses, combine it with <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> in a system known as the <a href="/wiki/Single_transferable_vote" title="Single transferable vote">single transferable vote</a>. <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_voting" title="Compulsory voting">Voting is compulsory</a> for all enrolled citizens 18 years and over in every jurisdiction,<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[200]</a></sup> as is enrolment.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[201]</a></sup> The party with majority support in the House of Representatives forms the government and its leader becomes Prime Minister. In cases where no party has majority support, the Governor-General has the constitutional power to appoint the Prime Minister and, if necessary, dismiss one that has lost the confidence of Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[202]</a></sup> Due to the relatively unique position of Australia operating as a Westminster Parliamentary democracy with an elected upper house, the system has sometimes been referred to as having a "Washminster mutation",<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[203]</a></sup> or as a <a href="/wiki/Semi-parliamentary_system" title="Semi-parliamentary system">Semi-parliamentary system</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ganghof_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ganghof-211">[204]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are two major political groups that usually form government, federally and in the states: the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Labor_Party" title="Australian Labor Party">Australian Labor Party</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Coalition_(Australia)" title="Coalition (Australia)">Coalition</a> which is a formal grouping of the <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_Australia" title="Liberal Party of Australia">Liberal Party</a> and its minor partner, the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_of_Australia" title="National Party of Australia">National Party</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[206]</a></sup> Within Australian political culture, the Coalition is considered <a href="/wiki/Centre-right" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-right">centre-right</a> and the Labor Party is considered <a href="/wiki/Centre-left" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-left">centre-left</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[207]</a></sup> Independent members and several minor parties have achieved representation in Australian parliaments, mostly in upper houses. The <a href="/wiki/Australian_Greens" title="Australian Greens">Australian Greens</a> are often considered the "third force" in politics, being the third largest party by both vote and membership.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[208]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/2019_Australian_federal_election" title="2019 Australian federal election">most recent federal election</a> was held on 18 May 2019 and resulted in the Coalition, led by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Scott_Morrison" title="Scott Morrison">Scott Morrison</a>, retaining <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Government of Australia">government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[209]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="States_and_territories">States and territories</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">States and territories of Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg/390px-Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg.png" decoding="async" width="390" height="390" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg/585px-Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg/780px-Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="791" data-file-height="790"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australia_states_and_territories_labelled.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Australia's states and territories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia has six states — <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> (NSW), <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> (QLD), <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">South Australia</a> (SA), <a href="/wiki/Tasmania" title="Tasmania">Tasmania</a> (TAS), <a href="/wiki/Victoria_(Australia)" title="Victoria (Australia)">Victoria</a> (VIC) and <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a> (WA) — and two major mainland territories—the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Capital_Territory" title="Australian Capital Territory">Australian Capital Territory</a> (ACT) and the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Territory" title="Northern Territory">Northern Territory</a> (NT). In most respects, these two territories function as states, except that the Commonwealth Parliament has the power to modify or repeal any legislation passed by the territory parliaments.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">[210]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under the constitution, the states essentially have <a href="/wiki/Plenary_power" title="Plenary power">plenary legislative power</a> to legislate on any subject, whereas the Commonwealth (federal) Parliament may legislate only within the subject areas enumerated under <a href="/wiki/Section_51_of_the_Australian_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Section 51 of the Australian Constitution">section 51</a>. For example, state parliaments have the power to legislate with respect to education, criminal law and state police, health, transport, and local government, but the Commonwealth Parliament does not have any specific power to legislate in these areas.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[211]</a></sup> However, Commonwealth laws prevail over state laws to the extent of the inconsistency.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[212]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Each state and major mainland territory has its own <a href="/wiki/Parliaments_of_the_Australian_states_and_territories" title="Parliaments of the Australian states and territories">parliament</a> — <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> in the Northern Territory, the ACT and Queensland, and bicameral in the other states. The states are sovereign entities, although subject to certain powers of the Commonwealth as defined by the Constitution. The lower houses are known as the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative Assembly">Legislative Assembly</a> (the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly" title="House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a> in South Australia and Tasmania); the upper houses are known as the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_council" title="Legislative council">Legislative Council</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of the government</a> in each state is the <a href="/wiki/Premiers_of_the_Australian_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Premiers of the Australian states">Premier</a> and in each territory the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Minister">Chief Minister</a>. The Queen is represented in each state by a <a href="/wiki/Governors_of_the_Australian_states" title="Governors of the Australian states">governor</a>; and in the Northern Territory, the <a href="/wiki/Administrator_of_the_Northern_Territory" title="Administrator of the Northern Territory">administrator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[213]</a></sup> In the Commonwealth, the Queen's representative is the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">governor-general</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[214]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Commonwealth Parliament also directly administers the external territories of <a href="/wiki/Ashmore_and_Cartier_Islands" title="Ashmore and Cartier Islands">Ashmore and Cartier Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Island" title="Christmas Island">Christmas Island</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cocos_(Keeling)_Islands" title="Cocos (Keeling) Islands">Cocos (Keeling) Islands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Coral_Sea_Islands" title="Coral Sea Islands">Coral Sea Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heard_Island_and_McDonald_Islands" title="Heard Island and McDonald Islands">Heard Island and McDonald Islands</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_claims_in_Antarctica" title="Territorial claims in Antarctica">claimed region</a> of <a href="/wiki/Australian_Antarctic_Territory" title="Australian Antarctic Territory">Australian Antarctic Territory</a>, as well as the internal <a href="/wiki/Jervis_Bay_Territory" title="Jervis Bay Territory">Jervis Bay Territory</a>, a naval base and sea port for the national capital in land that was formerly part of New South Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-CIAfactbook_200-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIAfactbook-200">[193]</a></sup> The external territory of <a href="/wiki/Norfolk_Island" title="Norfolk Island">Norfolk Island</a> previously exercised considerable autonomy under the <i>Norfolk Island Act 1979</i> through its own legislative assembly and an <a href="/wiki/List_of_administrative_heads_of_Norfolk_Island" title="List of administrative heads of Norfolk Island">Administrator</a> to represent the Queen.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[215]</a></sup> In 2015, the Commonwealth Parliament abolished self-government, integrating Norfolk Island into the Australian tax and welfare systems and replacing its legislative assembly with a council.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[216]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Macquarie_Island" title="Macquarie Island">Macquarie Island</a> is part of Tasmania,<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[217]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Lord_Howe_Island" title="Lord Howe Island">Lord Howe Island</a> of New South Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[218]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Australia" title="Foreign relations of Australia">Foreign relations of Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_(49649936152).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_%2849649936152%29.jpg/220px-Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_%2849649936152%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_%2849649936152%29.jpg/330px-Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_%2849649936152%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_%2849649936152%29.jpg/440px-Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_%2849649936152%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6483" data-file-height="4322"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Secretary_Pompeo_meets_with_Australian_Foreign_Minister_Payne_(49649936152).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Australia's <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Foreign_Affairs_(Australia)" title="Minister for Foreign Affairs (Australia)">Minister for Foreign Affairs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marise_Payne" title="Marise Payne">Marise Payne</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Over recent decades, <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Australia" title="Foreign relations of Australia">Australia's foreign relations</a> have been driven by a close association with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> through the <a href="/wiki/ANZUS" title="ANZUS">ANZUS</a> pact, and by a desire to develop relationships with Asia and the Pacific, particularly through <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Southeast_Asian_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Southeast Asian Nations">Association of Southeast Asian Nations</a> (ASEAN), the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Forum" title="Pacific Islands Forum">Pacific Islands Forum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Community" title="Pacific Community">Pacific Community</a>, of which Australia is a founding member. In 2005, Australia secured an inaugural seat at the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a> following its accession to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Amity_and_Cooperation_in_Southeast_Asia" title="Treaty of Amity and Cooperation in Southeast Asia">Treaty of Amity and Cooperation in Southeast Asia</a>, and in 2011 attended the <a href="/wiki/Sixth_East_Asia_Summit" title="Sixth East Asia Summit">Sixth East Asia Summit</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>. Australia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, in which the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Heads_of_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Commonwealth Heads of Government">Commonwealth Heads of Government</a> meetings provide the main forum for co-operation.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[219]</a></sup> Australia has pursued the cause of international <a href="/wiki/Trade_liberalisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade liberalisation">trade liberalisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[220]</a></sup> It led the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Cairns_Group" title="Cairns Group">Cairns Group</a> and <a href="/wiki/Asia-Pacific_Economic_Cooperation" title="Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation">Asia-Pacific Economic Cooperation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[222]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development</a> (OECD) and the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO),<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[224]</a></sup> and has pursued several major bilateral free trade agreements, most recently the <a href="/wiki/Australia%E2%80%93United_States_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Australia–United States Free Trade Agreement">Australia–United States Free Trade Agreement</a> <sup id="cite_ref-AUSdfat_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AUSdfat-232">[225]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Closer_Economic_Relations" title="Closer Economic Relations">Closer Economic Relations</a> with New Zealand,<sup id="cite_ref-CERdfat_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CERdfat-233">[226]</a></sup> with another free trade agreement being negotiated with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> — the <a href="/wiki/Australia%E2%80%93China_Free_Trade_Agreement" class="mw-redirect" title="Australia–China Free Trade Agreement">Australia–China Free Trade Agreement</a> — and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[227]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[228]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[229]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australia%E2%80%93Chile_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="Australia–Chile Free Trade Agreement">Australia–Chile Free Trade Agreement</a>, and as of November&nbsp;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> has put the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Partnership">Trans-Pacific Partnership</a> before parliament for ratification.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia maintains a deeply integrated relationship with neighbouring New Zealand, with free mobility of citizens between the two countries under the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Tasman_Travel_Arrangement" title="Trans-Tasman Travel Arrangement">Trans-Tasman Travel Arrangement</a> and free trade under the <a href="/wiki/Closer_Economic_Relations" title="Closer Economic Relations">Australia–New Zealand Closer Economic Relations Trade Agreement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[231]</a></sup> New Zealand, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> are the most favourably viewed countries in the world by <a href="/wiki/Australian_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian people">Australian people</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[233]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Along with New Zealand, the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, Australia is party to the <a href="/wiki/Five_Power_Defence_Arrangements" title="Five Power Defence Arrangements">Five Power Defence Arrangements</a>, a regional defence agreement. A founding member country of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, Australia is strongly committed to <a href="/wiki/Multilateralism" title="Multilateralism">multilateralism</a><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[234]</a></sup> and maintains an international aid program under which some 60 countries receive assistance. The 2005–2006 budget provides AU$2.5 <a href="/wiki/Billion" title="Billion">billion</a> for development assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-budget_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-budget-242">[235]</a></sup> Australia ranks fifteenth overall in the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Global_Development" title="Center for Global Development">Center for Global Development</a>'s 2012 <a href="/wiki/Commitment_to_Development_Index" title="Commitment to Development Index">Commitment to Development Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[236]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Australian_Defence_Force" title="Australian Defence Force">Australian Defence Force</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji,_Iraq,_Nov_15,_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Colour photograph of people wearing military uniforms standing in lines during a formal parade" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji%2C_Iraq%2C_Nov_15%2C_2017.jpg/220px-Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji%2C_Iraq%2C_Nov_15%2C_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji%2C_Iraq%2C_Nov_15%2C_2017.jpg/330px-Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji%2C_Iraq%2C_Nov_15%2C_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji%2C_Iraq%2C_Nov_15%2C_2017.jpg/440px-Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji%2C_Iraq%2C_Nov_15%2C_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_soldiers_attend_a_medals_parade_at_Camp_Taji,_Iraq,_Nov_15,_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Australian soldiers deployed to Iraq in 2017.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia's armed forces—the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Defence_Force" title="Australian Defence Force">Australian Defence Force</a> (ADF) — comprise the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Navy" title="Royal Australian Navy">Royal Australian Navy</a> (RAN), the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Army" title="Australian Army">Australian Army</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Australian_Air_Force" title="Royal Australian Air Force">Royal Australian Air Force</a> (RAAF), in total numbering 81,214 personnel (including 57,982 regulars and 23,232 reservists) as of November&nbsp;2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>. The titular role of <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-Chief" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander-in-Chief">Commander-in-Chief</a> is vested in the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">Governor-General</a>, who appoints a <a href="/wiki/Chief_of_the_Defence_Force_(Australia)" title="Chief of the Defence Force (Australia)">Chief of the Defence Force</a> from one of the armed services on the advice of the government.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">[237]</a></sup> In a <a href="/wiki/Diarchy" title="Diarchy">diarchy</a>, the CDF serves as co-chairman of the <a href="/wiki/Defence_Committee_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Defence Committee (Australia)">Defence Committee</a>, conjointly with the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Defence_(Australia)#Secretary_of_Defence" title="Department of Defence (Australia)">Secretary of Defence</a>, in the command and control of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Defence_Organisation" title="Australian Defence Organisation">Australian Defence Organisation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[238]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2016–2017 budget, defence spending comprised 2% of GDP, representing the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_military_expenditures" title="List of countries by military expenditures">12th largest defence budget</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">[239]</a></sup> Australia has been involved in <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and regional peacekeeping, disaster relief and armed conflict, including the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>; Australia <a href="/wiki/Current_Australian_Defence_Force_deployments" class="mw-redirect" title="Current Australian Defence Force deployments">currently has deployed</a> about 2,241 personnel in varying capacities to 12 international operations in areas including <a href="/wiki/Operation_Okra" title="Operation Okra">Iraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">Afghanistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[240]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Australia" title="Economy of Australia">Economy of Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Economic_history_of_Australia" title="Economic history of Australia">Economic history of Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Median_household_income_in_Australia_and_New_Zealand" title="Median household income in Australia and New Zealand">Median household income in Australia and New Zealand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Australia" title="Transport in Australia">Transport in Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg/260px-Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="260" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg/390px-Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg/520px-Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1190" data-file-height="808"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Australian_Energy_resources_and_major_export_ports_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Australian energy resources and major export ports map
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A wealthy country, Australia has a <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">market economy</a>, a high GDP per capita, and a relatively low rate of poverty. In terms of average wealth, Australia ranked second in the world after Switzerland from 2013 until 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-248">[241]</a></sup> In 2018, Australia overtook Switzerland and became the country with the highest average wealth.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-248">[241]</a></sup> Australia's <a href="/wiki/Relative_poverty" class="mw-redirect" title="Relative poverty">relative poverty</a> rate is 13.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[242]</a></sup> It was identified by the Credit Suisse Research Institute as the nation with the highest median wealth in the world and the second-highest average wealth per adult in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Credit_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Credit-250">[243]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">Australian dollar</a> is the currency for the nation, including Christmas Island, Cocos (Keeling) Islands, and Norfolk Island, as well as the independent <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Islands">Pacific Island states</a> of <a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>. With the 2006 merger of the Australian Stock Exchange and the Sydney Futures Exchange, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Securities_Exchange" title="Australian Securities Exchange">Australian Securities Exchange</a> became the ninth largest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">[244]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Ranked fifth in the <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a> (2017),<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">[245]</a></sup> Australia is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal)">world's 13th largest economy</a> and has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">tenth highest per capita GDP</a> (nominal) at US$55,692.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[246]</a></sup> The country was ranked third in the United Nations 2017 <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[247]</a></sup> Melbourne reached top spot for the fourth year in a row on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s 2014 list of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_most_livable_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="World's most livable cities">world's most liveable cities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">[248]</a></sup> followed by Adelaide, Sydney, and Perth in the fifth, seventh, and ninth places respectively. Total government debt in Australia is about A$190 <a href="/wiki/Billion" title="Billion">billion</a><sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">[249]</a></sup>—20% of <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[250]</a></sup> Australia has among the highest house prices and some of the highest <a href="/wiki/Household_debt" title="Household debt">household debt</a> levels in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[251]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Buildings and equipment of a large mining operation" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg/220px-Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg/330px-Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg/440px-Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Boddington_Gold_Mine_11.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Boddington_Gold_Mine" title="Boddington Gold Mine">Boddington Gold Mine</a> in Western Australia is the nation's largest <a href="/wiki/Open-pit_mining" title="Open-pit mining">open cut</a> mine.<sup id="cite_ref-boddingtonwa_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-boddingtonwa-259">[252]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>An emphasis on exporting commodities rather than manufactured goods has underpinned a significant increase in Australia's <a href="/wiki/Terms_of_trade" title="Terms of trade">terms of trade</a> since the start of the 21st century, due to rising commodity prices. <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_payments_of_Australia" title="Balance of payments of Australia">Australia has a balance of payments</a> that is more than 7% of GDP negative, and has had persistently large <a href="/wiki/Current_account_(balance_of_payments)" title="Current account (balance of payments)">current account</a> deficits for more than 50 years.<sup id="cite_ref-downwonder_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-downwonder-260">[253]</a></sup> Australia has grown at an average annual rate of 3.6% for over 15 years, in comparison to the OECD annual average of 2.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-downwonder_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-downwonder-260">[253]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia was the only advanced economy not to experience a recession due to the <a href="/wiki/Late-2000s_recession" class="mw-redirect" title="Late-2000s recession">global financial downturn</a> in 2008–2009.<sup id="cite_ref-IMFOutlook2010_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMFOutlook2010-261">[254]</a></sup> However, the economies of six of Australia's major trading partners were in recession, which in turn affected Australia, significantly hampering its economic growth.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[256]</a></sup> From 2012 to early 2013, Australia's national economy grew, but some non-mining states and Australia's non-mining economy experienced a recession.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[257]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[259]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hawke" title="Bob Hawke">Hawke Government</a> <a href="/wiki/Floating_exchange_rate" title="Floating exchange rate">floated</a> the Australian dollar in 1983 and partially deregulated the financial system.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[260]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Howard_Government" title="Howard Government">Howard Government</a> followed with a <a href="/wiki/WorkChoices" title="WorkChoices">partial deregulation of the labour market</a> and the further <a href="/wiki/Privatisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Privatisation">privatisation</a> of state-owned businesses, most notably in the <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Australia" title="Telecommunications in Australia">telecommunications</a> industry.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[261]</a></sup> The indirect tax system was substantially changed in July 2000 with the introduction of a 10% <a href="/wiki/Goods_and_Services_Tax_(Australia)" class="mw-redirect" title="Goods and Services Tax (Australia)">Goods and Services Tax</a> (GST).<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[262]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Taxation_in_Australia" title="Taxation in Australia">Australia's tax system</a>, personal and company <a href="/wiki/Income_tax_in_Australia" title="Income tax in Australia">income tax</a> are the main sources of government revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[263]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of September&nbsp;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, there were 12,640,800 people employed (either full- or part-time), with an unemployment rate of 5.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-ABSLabourForce_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABSLabourForce-271">[264]</a></sup> Data released in mid-November 2013 showed that the number of welfare recipients had grown by 55%. In 2007 228,621 <a href="/wiki/Newstart_Allowance" class="mw-redirect" title="Newstart Allowance">Newstart unemployment allowance</a> recipients were registered, a total that increased to 646,414 in March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[265]</a></sup> According to the Graduate Careers Survey, full-time employment for newly qualified professionals from various occupations has declined since 2011 but it increases for graduates three years after graduation.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[267]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Australia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> interest rates in Australia were set at a record low of 0.1%, targeting an inflation rate of 2 to 3%.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[268]</a></sup> The service sector of the economy, including tourism, education, and financial services, accounts for about 70% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[269]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mining_in_Australia" title="Mining in Australia">Rich in natural resources</a>, Australia is a major exporter of agricultural products, particularly wheat and wool, minerals such as iron-ore and gold, and energy in the forms of liquified natural gas and coal. Although <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Australia" title="Agriculture in Australia">agriculture</a> and natural resources account for only 3% and 5% of GDP respectively, they contribute substantially to export performance. Australia's largest export markets are <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a>, and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Year_Book_2005_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_Book_2005-277">[270]</a></sup> Australia is the world's fourth largest exporter of wine, and the wine industry contributes A$5.5 billion per year to the nation's economy.<sup id="cite_ref-wineaustralia1_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wineaustralia1-278">[271]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Access to <a href="/wiki/Biocapacity" title="Biocapacity">biocapacity</a> in Australia is much higher than world average. In 2016, Australia had 12.3 global hectares<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-279">[272]</a></sup> of biocapacity per person within its territory, much more than the world average of 1.6 global hectares per person.<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">[273]</a></sup> In 2016 Australia used 6.6 global hectares of biocapacity per person – their <a href="/wiki/Ecological_footprint" title="Ecological footprint">ecological footprint</a> of consumption. This means they use half as much biocapacity as Australia contains. As a result, Australia is running a biocapacity reserve.<sup id="cite_ref-footprintdata_279-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footprintdata-279">[272]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2020 the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Council_of_Social_Service" title="Australian Council of Social Service">Australian Council of Social Service</a> released a report stating that relative poverty was growing in Australia, with an estimated 3.2&nbsp;million people, or 13.6% of the population, living below an internationally accepted relative poverty threshold of 50% of a country's median income. It also estimated that there were 774,000 (17.7%) children under the age of 15 in relative poverty.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[274]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[275]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demography_of_Australia" title="Demography of Australia">Demography of Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Australia_by_population" title="List of cities in Australia by population">List of cities in Australia by population</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="A beach populated by people; a city can be seen in the horizon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg/220px-Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg/330px-Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg/440px-Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5598" data-file-height="3318"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gold_Coast_skyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Australia has one of the world's most highly urbanised populations with the majority living in metropolitan cities on the coast, such as <a href="/wiki/Gold_Coast,_Queensland" title="Gold Coast, Queensland">Gold Coast</a>, Queensland.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia has an average <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> of 3.4 persons per square kilometre of total land area, which makes it is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by population density">most sparsely populated countries in the world</a>. The population is heavily concentrated on the east coast, and in particular in the south-eastern region between <a href="/wiki/South_East_Queensland" title="South East Queensland">South East Queensland</a> to the north-east and <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a> to the south-west.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[276]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia is highly urbanised, with 67% of the population living in the Greater Capital City Statistical Areas (metropolitan areas of the state and mainland territorial capital cities) in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[277]</a></sup> Metropolitan areas with more than one million inhabitants are <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brisbane" title="Brisbane">Brisbane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">Adelaide</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[278]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In common with many other developed countries, Australia is experiencing a demographic shift towards an older population, with more retirees and fewer people of working age. In 2018 the <a href="/wiki/Median_age" class="mw-redirect" title="Median age">average age</a> of the Australian population was 38.8 years.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">[279]</a></sup> In 2015, 2.15% of the Australian population <a href="/wiki/Australian_diaspora" title="Australian diaspora">lived overseas</a>, one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_immigrant_population#UN_2015_report:_emigrant_population" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by immigrant population">lowest proportions</a> worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[280]</a></sup> </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry_and_immigration">Ancestry and immigration</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Immigration_to_Australia" title="Immigration to Australia">Immigration to Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Australians" title="European Australians">European Australians</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous Australians</a>
      </div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float:right;"> 
       <caption>
        Country of birth (2020)<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[282]</a></sup>

         <td>7,653,990 </td>

      <p>Between 1788 and the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, the vast majority of settlers and immigrants came from the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Celtic_Australians" title="Anglo-Celtic Australians">British Isles</a> (principally <a href="/wiki/English_Australians" title="English Australians">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_Australians" title="Irish Australians">Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Australians" title="Scottish Australians">Scotland</a>), although there was significant immigration from <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Australians" title="Chinese Australians">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_Australians" title="German Australians">Germany</a> during the 19th century. In the decades immediately following the Second World War, Australia received a <a href="/wiki/Post-war_immigration_to_Australia" title="Post-war immigration to Australia">large wave of immigration</a> from across <a href="/wiki/European_Australians" title="European Australians">Europe</a>, with many more immigrants arriving from <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a> than in previous decades. Since the end of the <a href="/wiki/White_Australia_policy" title="White Australia policy">White Australia policy</a> in 1973, Australia has pursued an official policy of <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multiculturalism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[283]</a></sup> and there has been a large and continuing wave of immigration from across the world, with <a href="/wiki/Asian_Australians" title="Asian Australians">Asia</a> being the largest source of immigrants in the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-homeaffairs.gov.au_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-homeaffairs.gov.au-292">[284]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today, Australia has the world's <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_immigrant_population" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by immigrant population">eighth-largest</a> immigrant population, with immigrants accounting for 30% of the population, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states_and_dependent_territories_by_immigrant_population" title="List of sovereign states and dependent territories by immigrant population">highest proportion</a> among major <a href="/wiki/Western_world" title="Western world">Western</a> nations.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-32">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[285]</a></sup> 160,323 permanent immigrants were admitted to Australia in 2018–2019 (excluding <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-homeaffairs.gov.au_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-homeaffairs.gov.au-292">[284]</a></sup> whilst there was a net population gain of 239,600 people from all permanent and temporary immigration in that year.<sup id="cite_ref-immig_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immig-294">[286]</a></sup> The majority of immigrants are skilled,<sup id="cite_ref-homeaffairs.gov.au_292-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-homeaffairs.gov.au-292">[284]</a></sup> but the immigration program includes categories for family members and <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-immig_294-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-immig-294">[286]</a></sup> In 2019, the largest foreign-born populations were those born in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> (3.9%), <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a> (2.7%), <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (2.6%), New Zealand (2.2%), the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> (1.2%) and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> (1%).<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto1-32">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the 2016 Australian census, the most commonly nominated ancestries were:<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[N 9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2071.0_diversity_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2071.0_diversity-296">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[288]</a></sup> </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 12em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/wiki/English_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="English Australian">English</a> (36.1%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Australians" title="Australians">Australian</a> (33.5%)<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[N 10]</a></sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Irish_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Australian">Irish</a> (11.0%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Scottish_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish Australian">Scottish</a> (9.3%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese Australian">Chinese</a> (5.6%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Italian_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Italian Australian">Italian</a> (4.6%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/German_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="German Australian">German</a> (4.5%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Indian_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Indian Australian">Indian</a> (2.8%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous Australian">Indigenous</a> (2.8%)<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[N 11]</a></sup></li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Greek_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Australian">Greek</a> (1.8%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Dutch_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Australian">Dutch</a> (1.6%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Filipino_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino Australian">Filipino</a> (1.4%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Vietnamese Australian">Vietnamese</a> (1.4%)</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Lebanese_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanese Australian">Lebanese</a> (1%)</li>
       </ul>
      </div> 
      <p>At the 2016 census, 649,171 people (2.8% of the total population) identified as being <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous</a> — <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">Aboriginal Australians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait_Islanders" title="Torres Strait Islanders">Torres Strait Islanders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[N 12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[290]</a></sup> Indigenous Australians experience higher than average rates of imprisonment and unemployment, lower levels of education, and life expectancies for males and females that are, respectively, 11 and 17 years lower than those of non-indigenous Australians.<sup id="cite_ref-Year_Book_2005_277-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_Book_2005-277">[270]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[291]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[292]</a></sup> Some remote Indigenous communities have been described as having "<a href="/wiki/Failed_state" title="Failed state">failed state</a>"-like conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[293]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="***REMOVED***">Language</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Australia" title="Languages of Australia">Languages of Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Although Australia has no official language, English is the <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> national language.<sup id="cite_ref-language_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-language-3">[2]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Australian_English" title="Australian English">Australian English</a> is a major variety of the language with a distinctive accent and lexicon,<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[294]</a></sup> and differs slightly from other varieties of English in grammar and spelling.<sup id="cite_ref-Fourth_Edition_2005_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fourth_Edition_2005-307">[295]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/General_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="General Australian">General Australian</a> serves as the standard dialect.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[296]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2016 census, English is the only language spoken in the home for 72.7% of the population. The next most common languages spoken at home are <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin</a> (2.5%), <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> (1.4%), <a href="/wiki/Cantonese" title="Cantonese">Cantonese</a> (1.2%), <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a> (1.2%) and <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> (1.2%).<sup id="cite_ref-2071.0_diversity_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2071.0_diversity-296">[287]</a></sup> Over 250 <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australian_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous Australian languages">Indigenous Australian languages</a> are thought to have existed at the time of first European contact,<sup id="cite_ref-Romaine1991_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Romaine1991-309">[297]</a></sup> of which fewer than twenty are still in daily use by all age groups.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[298]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nilsr_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nilsr-311">[299]</a></sup> About 110 others are spoken exclusively by older people.<sup id="cite_ref-nilsr_311-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nilsr-311">[299]</a></sup> At the time of the 2006 census, 52,000 Indigenous Australians, representing 12% of the Indigenous population, reported that they spoke an Indigenous language at home.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[300]</a></sup> Australia has a <a href="/wiki/Sign_language" title="Sign language">sign language</a> known as <a href="/wiki/Auslan" title="Auslan">Auslan</a>, which is the main language of about 10,112 deaf people who reported that they spoke Auslan language at home in the 2016 census.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[301]</a></sup> </p>
