       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>Australia has no <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>; Section 116 of the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Constitution">Australian Constitution</a> prohibits the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Government_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Government of Australia">federal government</a> from making any law to establish any religion, impose any religious observance, or prohibit the free exercise of any religion.<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[303]</a></sup> In the 2016 census, 52.1% of Australians were counted as <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>, including 22.6% as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Australia">Catholic</a> and 13.3% as <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a>; 30.1% of the population reported having "<a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_Australia" title="Irreligion in Australia">no religion</a>"; 8.2% identify with non-Christian religions, the largest of these being <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (2.6%), followed by <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (2.4%), <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (1.9%), <a href="/wiki/Sikhism_in_Australia" title="Sikhism in Australia">Sikhism</a> (0.5%) and <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> (0.4%). The remaining 9.7% of the population did not provide an adequate answer. Those who reported having no religion increased conspicuously from 19% in 2006 to 22% in 2011 to 30.1% in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-auto3_314-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto3-314">[302]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Before European settlement, the animist beliefs of Australia's indigenous people had been practised for many thousands of years. Mainland Aboriginal Australians' spirituality is known as <a href="/wiki/The_Dreaming" title="The Dreaming">the Dreaming</a> and it places a heavy emphasis on belonging to the land. The collection of stories that it contains shaped Aboriginal law and customs. <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australian_art" title="Indigenous Australian art">Aboriginal art</a>, story and dance continue to draw on these spiritual traditions. The spirituality and customs of <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait_Islanders" title="Torres Strait Islanders">Torres Strait Islanders</a>, who inhabit the islands between Australia and New Guinea, reflected their Melanesian origins and dependence on the sea. The 1996 Australian census counted more than 7000 respondents as followers of a traditional Aboriginal religion.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[304]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/First_Fleet" title="First Fleet">First Fleet</a> of British ships in 1788, Christianity has become the major religion practised in Australia. Christian churches have played an integral role in the development of education, health and welfare services in Australia. For much of Australian history, the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> (now known as the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Australia" title="Anglican Church of Australia">Anglican Church of Australia</a>) was the largest religious denomination, with a large <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> minority. However, multicultural immigration has contributed to a steep decline in its relative position since the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Australia" title="Islam in Australia">Islam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Australia" title="Buddhism in Australia">Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Australia" title="Hinduism in Australia">Hinduism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sikhism_in_Australia" title="Sikhism in Australia">Sikhism</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the Jews in Australia">Judaism</a> have all grown in Australia over the past half-century.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[305]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia has one of the lowest levels of religious adherence in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[306]</a></sup> In 2018, 13% of women and 10% of men reported attending church at least weekly.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[307]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Health_care_in_Australia" title="Health care in Australia">Health care in Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia's life expectancy is the fourth highest in the world for males and the third highest for females.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[308]</a></sup> Life expectancy in Australia in 2014–2016 was 80.4 years for males and 84.6 years for females.<sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">[309]</a></sup> Australia has the highest rates of skin cancer in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[310]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Tobacco_smoking" title="Tobacco smoking">cigarette smoking</a> is the largest preventable cause of death and disease, responsible for 7.8% of the total mortality and disease. Ranked second in preventable causes is <a href="/wiki/Hypertension" title="Hypertension">hypertension</a> at 7.6%, with obesity third at 7.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[311]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-324" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-324">[312]</a></sup> Australia ranks 35th in the world<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">[313]</a></sup> and near the top of <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed nations</a> for its proportion of <a href="/wiki/Obesity_in_Australia" title="Obesity in Australia">obese</a> adults<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[314]</a></sup> and nearly two thirds (63%) of its adult population is either overweight or obese.<sup id="cite_ref-aihw_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aihw-327">[315]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Total expenditure on health (including private sector spending) is around 9.8% of GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">[316]</a></sup> Australia introduced <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">universal health care</a> in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-medicbrief_329-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medicbrief-329">[317]</a></sup> Known as <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(Australia)" title="Medicare (Australia)">Medicare</a>, it is now nominally funded by an income tax surcharge known as the <a href="/wiki/Medicare_levy" class="mw-redirect" title="Medicare levy">Medicare levy</a>, currently at 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">[318]</a></sup> The states manage hospitals and attached outpatient services, while the Commonwealth funds the <a href="/wiki/Pharmaceutical_Benefits_Scheme" title="Pharmaceutical Benefits Scheme">Pharmaceutical Benefits Scheme</a> (subsidising the costs of medicines) and general practice.<sup id="cite_ref-medicbrief_329-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-medicbrief-329">[317]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Australia" title="Education in Australia">Education in Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:JCMSR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/JCMSR.jpg/220px-JCMSR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/JCMSR.jpg/330px-JCMSR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/JCMSR.jpg/440px-JCMSR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1463" data-file-height="1097"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:JCMSR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Five Australian universities rank in the top 50 of the <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i>, including the <a href="/wiki/Australian_National_University" title="Australian National University">Australian National University</a> (19th).<sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">[319]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>School attendance, or registration for home schooling,<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[320]</a></sup> is compulsory throughout Australia. Education is the responsibility of the individual states and territories<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[321]</a></sup> so the rules vary between states, but in general children are required to attend school from the age of about 5 until about 16.<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">[322]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">[323]</a></sup> In some states (e.g., Western Australia, the Northern Territory and New South Wales), children aged 16–17 are required to either attend school or participate in vocational training, such as an <a href="/wiki/Apprenticeship" title="Apprenticeship">apprenticeship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[325]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-338" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-338">[326]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[327]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia has an adult literacy rate that was estimated to be 99% in 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-cialittab_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cialittab-340">[328]</a></sup> However, a 2011–2012 report for the Australian Bureau of Statistics reported that Tasmania has a literacy and numeracy rate of only 50%.<sup id="cite_ref-341" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-341">[329]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia has 37 government-funded universities and three private universities, as well as a number of other specialist institutions that provide approved courses at the higher education level.<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[330]</a></sup> The OECD places Australia among the most expensive nations to attend university.<sup id="cite_ref-343" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-343">[331]</a></sup> There is a state-based system of vocational training, known as <a href="/wiki/Technical_and_further_education" title="Technical and further education">TAFE</a>, and many trades conduct apprenticeships for training new tradespeople.<sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[332]</a></sup> About 58% of Australians aged from 25 to 64 have vocational or tertiary qualifications,<sup id="cite_ref-Year_Book_2005_277-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Year_Book_2005-277">[270]</a></sup> and the tertiary graduation rate of 49% is the highest among OECD countries. 30.9% of Australia's population has attained a higher education qualification, which is among the highest percentages in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-345" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-345">[333]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[334]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[335]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia has the highest ratio of <a href="/wiki/International_students_in_Australia" title="International students in Australia">international students</a> per head of population in the world by a large margin, with 812,000 international students enrolled in the nation's universities and vocational institutions in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[336]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[337]</a></sup> Accordingly, in 2019, international students represented on average 26.7% of the student bodies of Australian universities. International education therefore represents one of the country's largest exports and has a pronounced influence on the country's demographics, with a significant proportion of international students remaining in Australia after graduation on various skill and employment visas.<sup id="cite_ref-350" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-350">[338]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Australia" title="Culture of Australia">Culture of Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Ornate white building with an elevated dome in the middle, fronted by a golden fountain and orange flowers" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg/220px-Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg/330px-Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg/440px-Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1856" data-file-height="1280"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Royal_exhibition_building_tulips_straight.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Exhibition_Building" title="Royal Exhibition Building">Royal Exhibition Building</a> in Melbourne was the first building in Australia to be listed as a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[339]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 1788, the primary influence behind Australian culture has been <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Celtic" title="Anglo-Celtic">Anglo-Celtic</a> <a href="/wiki/Western_culture" title="Western culture">Western culture</a>, with some <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australians" title="Indigenous Australians">Indigenous</a> influences.<sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">[340]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-353" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-353">[341]</a></sup> The divergence and evolution that has occurred in the ensuing centuries has resulted in a distinctive Australian culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Davison_pp98–9_354-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davison_pp98–9-354">[342]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-355" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-355">[343]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States" title="Culture of the United States">culture of the United States</a> has served as a significant influence, particularly through television and cinema. Other cultural influences come from neighbouring Asian countries, and through large-scale immigration from non-English-speaking nations.<sup id="cite_ref-356" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-356">[344]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts">Arts</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Australian_art" title="Australian art">Australian art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australian_literature" title="Australian literature">Australian literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Australia" title="Theatre of Australia">Theatre of Australia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Australia" title="Dance in Australia">Dance in Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Australia has over 100,000 <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_Australian_art#Rock_painting" title="Indigenous Australian art">Aboriginal rock art</a> sites,<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">[345]</a></sup> and traditional designs, patterns and stories infuse <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Indigenous_Australian_art" title="Contemporary Indigenous Australian art">contemporary Indigenous Australian art</a>, "the last great art movement of the 20th century" according to critic <a href="/wiki/Robert_Hughes_(critic)" title="Robert Hughes (critic)">Robert Hughes</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[346]</a></sup> its exponents include <a href="/wiki/Emily_Kame_Kngwarreye" title="Emily Kame Kngwarreye">Emily Kame Kngwarreye</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[347]</a></sup> Early colonial artists showed a fascination with the unfamiliar land.<sup id="cite_ref-art_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art-360">[348]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Impressionism" title="Impressionism">impressionistic</a> works of <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Streeton" title="Arthur Streeton">Arthur Streeton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Roberts" title="Tom Roberts">Tom Roberts</a> and other members of the 19th-century <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg_School" title="Heidelberg School">Heidelberg School</a>—the first "distinctively Australian" movement in Western art—gave expression to nationalist sentiments in the lead-up to Federation.<sup id="cite_ref-art_360-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art-360">[348]</a></sup> While the school remained influential into the 1900s, <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modernists</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Preston" title="Margaret Preston">Margaret Preston</a>, and, later, <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Nolan" title="Sidney Nolan">Sidney Nolan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Boyd" title="Arthur Boyd">Arthur Boyd</a>, explored new artistic trends.<sup id="cite_ref-art_360-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art-360">[348]</a></sup> The landscape remained a central subject matter for <a href="/wiki/Fred_Williams_(artist)" title="Fred Williams (artist)">Fred Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brett_Whiteley" title="Brett Whiteley">Brett Whiteley</a> and other post-war artists whose works, eclectic in style yet uniquely Australian, moved between the <a href="/wiki/Figurative_art" title="Figurative art">figurative</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Abstract_art" title="Abstract art">abstract</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-art_360-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-art-360">[348]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[349]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Gallery_of_Australia" title="National Gallery of Australia">national</a> and state galleries maintain collections of local and international art.<sup id="cite_ref-362" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-362">[350]</a></sup> Australia has one of the world's highest attendances of art galleries and museums per head of population.<sup id="cite_ref-363" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-363">[351]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg/220px-Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg/330px-Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg/440px-Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1350"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sidney_Nolan_Snake.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sidney_Nolan" title="Sidney Nolan">Sidney Nolan</a>'s <i>Snake</i> mural (1970), held at the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Old_and_New_Art" title="Museum of Old and New Art">Museum of Old and New Art</a> in Hobart, Tasmania, is inspired by the Aboriginal creation myth of the <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Serpent" title="Rainbow Serpent">Rainbow Serpent</a>, as well as desert flowers in bloom after a drought.<sup id="cite_ref-364" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-364">[352]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Australian_literature" title="Australian literature">Australian literature</a> grew slowly in the decades following European settlement though Indigenous <a href="/wiki/Oral_tradition" title="Oral tradition">oral traditions</a>, many of which have since been recorded in writing, are much older.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[353]</a></sup> In the 1870s, <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lindsay_Gordon" title="Adam Lindsay Gordon">Adam Lindsay Gordon</a> posthumously became the first Australian poet to attain a wide readership. Following in his footsteps, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Lawson" title="Henry Lawson">Henry Lawson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Banjo_Paterson" title="Banjo Paterson">Banjo Paterson</a> captured the experience of <a href="/wiki/Australian_bush" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian bush">the bush</a> using a distinctive Australian vocabulary.<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[354]</a></sup> Their works are still popular; Paterson's <a href="/wiki/Bush_poetry" class="mw-redirect" title="Bush poetry">bush poem</a> "<a href="/wiki/Waltzing_Matilda" title="Waltzing Matilda">Waltzing Matilda</a>" (1895) is regarded as Australia's unofficial national anthem.<sup id="cite_ref-367" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-367">[355]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Miles_Franklin" title="Miles Franklin">Miles Franklin</a> is the namesake of Australia's <a href="/wiki/Miles_Franklin_Award" title="Miles Franklin Award">most prestigious literary prize</a>, awarded annually to the best novel about Australian life.<sup id="cite_ref-368" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-368">[356]</a></sup> Its first recipient, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_White" title="Patrick White">Patrick White</a>, went on to win the <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Literature" title="Nobel Prize in Literature">Nobel Prize in Literature</a> in 1973.<sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[357]</a></sup> Australian <a href="/wiki/Man_Booker_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Man Booker Prize">Booker Prize</a> winners include <a href="/wiki/Peter_Carey_(novelist)" title="Peter Carey (novelist)">Peter Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Keneally" title="Thomas Keneally">Thomas Keneally</a> and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Flanagan" title="Richard Flanagan">Richard Flanagan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-370" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-370">[358]</a></sup> Authors <a href="/wiki/David_Malouf" title="David Malouf">David Malouf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germaine_Greer" title="Germaine Greer">Germaine Greer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Helen_Garner" title="Helen Garner">Helen Garner</a>, playwright <a href="/wiki/David_Williamson" title="David Williamson">David Williamson</a> and poet <a href="/wiki/Les_Murray_(poet)" title="Les Murray (poet)">Les Murray</a> are also renowned.<sup id="cite_ref-Davison_p394_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davison_p394-371">[359]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JT77_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JT77-372">[360]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Many of Australia's performing arts companies receive funding through the federal government's <a href="/wiki/Australia_Council_for_the_Arts" title="Australia Council for the Arts">Australia Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[361]</a></sup> There is a symphony orchestra in each state,<sup id="cite_ref-374" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-374">[362]</a></sup> and a national opera company, <a href="/wiki/Opera_Australia" title="Opera Australia">Opera Australia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">[363]</a></sup> well known for its famous <a href="/wiki/Soprano" title="Soprano">soprano</a> <a href="/wiki/Joan_Sutherland" title="Joan Sutherland">Joan Sutherland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-376" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-376">[364]</a></sup> At the beginning of the 20th century, <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Melba" title="Nellie Melba">Nellie Melba</a> was one of the world's leading opera singers.<sup id="cite_ref-377" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-377">[365]</a></sup> Ballet and dance are represented by <a href="/wiki/The_Australian_Ballet" title="The Australian Ballet">The Australian Ballet</a> and various state companies. Each state has a publicly funded theatre company.<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">[366]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Australia" title="Cinema of Australia">Cinema of Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Television_in_Australia" title="Television in Australia">Television in Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Australia" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Australia">Media of Australia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Australia" title="Music of Australia">Music of Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg/220px-The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg/330px-The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg/440px-The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1058"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang_1906.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Actor playing the <a href="/wiki/Bushranger" title="Bushranger">bushranger</a> <a href="/wiki/Ned_Kelly" title="Ned Kelly">Ned Kelly</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang" title="The Story of the Kelly Gang">The Story of the Kelly Gang</a></i> (1906), the world's first feature-length narrative film
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_the_Kelly_Gang" title="The Story of the Kelly Gang">The Story of the Kelly Gang</a></i> (1906), the world's first <a href="/wiki/Feature_film" title="Feature film">feature-length</a> narrative film, spurred a boom in <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Australia" title="Cinema of Australia">Australian cinema</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Silent_film" title="Silent film">silent film</a> era.<sup id="cite_ref-379" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-379">[367]</a></sup> After World War I, <a href="/wiki/Hollywood" title="Hollywood">Hollywood</a> monopolised the industry,<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">[368]</a></sup> and by the 1960s Australian film production had effectively ceased.<sup id="cite_ref-381" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-381">[369]</a></sup> With the benefit of government support, the <a href="/wiki/Australian_New_Wave" title="Australian New Wave">Australian New Wave</a> of the 1970s brought provocative and successful films, many exploring themes of national identity, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Wake_in_Fright" title="Wake in Fright">Wake in Fright</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Gallipoli_(1981_film)" title="Gallipoli (1981 film)">Gallipoli</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-382" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-382">[370]</a></sup> while <i><a href="/wiki/Crocodile_Dundee" title="Crocodile Dundee">Crocodile Dundee</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Ozploitation" title="Ozploitation">Ozploitation</a> movement's <i><a href="/wiki/Mad_Max_(franchise)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mad Max (franchise)">Mad Max</a></i> series became international blockbusters.<sup id="cite_ref-383" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-383">[371]</a></sup> In a film market flooded with foreign content, Australian films delivered a 7.7% share of the local box office in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-384" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-384">[372]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/AACTA_Awards" title="AACTA Awards">AACTAs</a> are Australia's premier film and television awards, and notable <a href="/wiki/List_of_Australian_Academy_Award_winners_and_nominees" title="List of Australian Academy Award winners and nominees">Academy Award winners from Australia</a> include <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_Rush" title="Geoffrey Rush">Geoffrey Rush</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Kidman" title="Nicole Kidman">Nicole Kidman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cate_Blanchett" title="Cate Blanchett">Cate Blanchett</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heath_Ledger" title="Heath Ledger">Heath Ledger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[373]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia has two public broadcasters (the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Australian Broadcasting Corporation">Australian Broadcasting Corporation</a> and the multicultural <a href="/wiki/Special_Broadcasting_Service" title="Special Broadcasting Service">Special Broadcasting Service</a>), three commercial television networks, several pay-TV services,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-386">[374]</a></sup> and numerous public, non-profit television and radio stations. Each major city has at least one daily newspaper,<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_386-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-386">[374]</a></sup> and there are two national daily newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian" title="The Australian">The Australian</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Australian_Financial_Review" class="mw-redirect" title="The Australian Financial Review">The Australian Financial Review</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_386-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-386">[374]</a></sup> In 2010, <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> placed Australia 18th on a list of 178 countries ranked by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">press freedom</a>, behind New Zealand (8th) but ahead of the United Kingdom (19th) and United States (20th).<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[375]</a></sup> This relatively low ranking is primarily because of the limited diversity of commercial media ownership in Australia;<sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[376]</a></sup> most print media are under the control of <a href="/wiki/News_Corporation_(1980%E2%80%932013)" class="mw-redirect" title="News Corporation (1980–2013)">News Corporation</a> and, after <a href="/wiki/Fairfax_Media" title="Fairfax Media">Fairfax Media</a> was merged with Nine, <a href="/wiki/Nine_Entertainment_Co." class="mw-redirect" title="Nine Entertainment Co.">Nine Entertainment Co.</a><sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[377]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Australian_cuisine" title="Australian cuisine">Australian cuisine</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg/220px-Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg/330px-Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg/440px-Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2646" data-file-height="2094"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pavlova_garnished_with_cream_and_strawberries.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The meringue-based <a href="/wiki/Pavlova_(cake)" title="Pavlova (cake)">pavlova</a> is generally eaten at Christmas time.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most Indigenous Australian groups subsisted on a simple <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer_diet" class="mw-redirect" title="Hunter-gatherer diet">hunter-gatherer diet</a> of native fauna and flora, otherwise called <a href="/wiki/Bush_tucker" title="Bush tucker">bush tucker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-390" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-390">[378]</a></sup> The first settlers introduced <a href="/wiki/British_cuisine" title="British cuisine">British food</a> to the continent, much of which is now considered typical Australian food, such as the <a href="/wiki/Sunday_roast" title="Sunday roast">Sunday roast</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-food_391-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-food-391">[379]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-f2_392-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-f2-392">[380]</a></sup> Multicultural immigration transformed Australian cuisine; post-World War II European migrants, particularly from the Mediterranean, helped to build a thriving Australian <a href="/wiki/Coffee_culture" title="Coffee culture">coffee culture</a>, and the influence of <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Asia" title="Culture of Asia">Asian cultures</a> has led to Australian variants of their staple foods, such as the <a href="/wiki/Chinese_cuisine" title="Chinese cuisine">Chinese</a>-inspired <a href="/wiki/Dim_sim" title="Dim sim">dim sim</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chiko_Roll" title="Chiko Roll">Chiko Roll</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[381]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vegemite" title="Vegemite">Vegemite</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pavlova_(food)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pavlova (food)">pavlova</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lamington" title="Lamington">lamingtons</a> and <a href="/wiki/Meat_pie_(Australia_and_New_Zealand)" title="Meat pie (Australia and New Zealand)">meat pies</a> are regarded as iconic Australian foods.<sup id="cite_ref-394" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-394">[382]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Australian_wine" title="Australian wine">Australian wine</a> is produced mainly in the southern, cooler parts of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-395" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-395">[383]</a></sup> Australia is also known for its <a href="/wiki/Coffeehouse" title="Coffeehouse">cafe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coffee_culture" title="Coffee culture">coffee culture</a> in <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban centres</a>, which has influenced coffee culture abroad, including <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">[384]</a></sup> Australia was responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Flat_white" title="Flat white">flat white</a> coffee–purported to have originated in a Sydney cafe in the mid-1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-397" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-397">[385]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport_and_recreation">Sport and recreation</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Australia" title="Sport in Australia">Sport in Australia</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg/220px-2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg/330px-2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg/440px-2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7386" data-file-height="3918"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2017_AFL_Grand_Final_panorama_during_national_anthem.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cricket_Ground" title="Melbourne Cricket Ground">Melbourne Cricket Ground</a> is strongly associated with the history and development of <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a>, Australia's two most popular spectator sports.<sup id="cite_ref-398" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-398">[386]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football" title="Football">football</a> are the predominate sports in Australia during the summer and winter months, respectively. Australia is unique in that it has professional leagues for <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Australia" title="Football in Australia">four football codes</a>. Originating in Melbourne in the 1850s, <a href="/wiki/Australian_rules_football" title="Australian rules football">Australian rules football</a> is the most popular code in all states except New South Wales and Queensland, where <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> holds sway, followed by <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>; the imaginary border separating areas where Australian rules football dominates from those were the two rugby codes prevail is known as the <a href="/wiki/Barassi_Line" title="Barassi Line">Barassi Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-researchgate_399-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchgate-399">[387]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Soccer</a>, while ranked fourth in popularity and resources, has the highest overall participation rates.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">[388]</a></sup> Cricket is popular across all borders and has been regarded by many Australians as the <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national sport</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_cricket_team" title="Australia national cricket team">Australian national cricket team</a> competed against <a href="/wiki/England_cricket_team" title="England cricket team">England</a> in the first <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">Test</a> match (1877) and the first <a href="/wiki/One_Day_International" title="One Day International">One Day International</a> (1971), and against <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand cricket team">New Zealand</a> in the first <a href="/wiki/Twenty20_International" title="Twenty20 International">Twenty20 International</a> (2004), winning all three games. It has also participated in every edition of the <a href="/wiki/Cricket_World_Cup" title="Cricket World Cup">Cricket World Cup</a>, winning the tournament a record five times.<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">[389]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia is also notable for water-based sports, such as swimming and <a href="/wiki/Surfing_in_Australia" title="Surfing in Australia">surfing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">[390]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Surf_lifesaving" title="Surf lifesaving">surf lifesaving</a> movement originated in Australia, and the volunteer lifesaver is one of the country's icons.<sup id="cite_ref-403" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-403">[391]</a></sup> Nationally, other popular sports include horse racing, basketball, and motor racing. The annual <a href="/wiki/Melbourne_Cup" title="Melbourne Cup">Melbourne Cup</a> horse race and the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_to_Hobart_Yacht_Race" title="Sydney to Hobart Yacht Race">Sydney to Hobart</a> yacht race attract intense interest.<sup id="cite_ref-404" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-404">[392]</a></sup> In 2016, the Australian Sports Commission revealed that swimming, cycling and soccer are the three most popular participation sports.<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">[393]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-406" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-406">[394]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Australia is one of five nations to have participated in every <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> of the modern era,<sup id="cite_ref-407" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-407">[395]</a></sup> and has hosted the Games twice: <a href="/wiki/1956_Summer_Olympics" title="1956 Summer Olympics">1956</a> in Melbourne and <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000</a> in Sydney.<sup id="cite_ref-Davison_pp479-80_408-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Davison_pp479-80-408">[396]</a></sup> Australia has also participated in every <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Games" title="Commonwealth Games">Commonwealth Games</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-409" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-409">[397]</a></sup> hosting the event in <a href="/wiki/1938_British_Empire_Games" title="1938 British Empire Games">1938</a>, <a href="/wiki/1962_British_Empire_and_Commonwealth_Games" title="1962 British Empire and Commonwealth Games">1962</a>, <a href="/wiki/1982_Commonwealth_Games" title="1982 Commonwealth Games">1982</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_Commonwealth_Games" title="2006 Commonwealth Games">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2018_Commonwealth_Games" title="2018 Commonwealth Games">2018</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">[398]</a></sup> Australia made its inaugural appearance at the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Games" title="Pacific Games">Pacific Games</a> in <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_Games" title="2015 Pacific Games">2015</a>. As well as being a regular <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> participant, Australia has won the <a href="/wiki/OFC_Nations_Cup" title="OFC Nations Cup">OFC Nations Cup</a> four times and the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a> once—the only country to have won championships in two different FIFA confederations.<sup id="cite_ref-411" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-411">[399]</a></sup> In June 2020, Australia won <a href="/wiki/Australia%E2%80%93New_Zealand_2023_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup_bid" title="Australia–New Zealand 2023 FIFA Women's World Cup bid">its bid</a> to co-host the <a href="/wiki/2023_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2023 FIFA Women's World Cup">2023 FIFA Women's World Cup</a> with New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-412" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-412">[400]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-413" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-413">[401]</a></sup> The country regularly competes among the world elite basketball teams as it is among the global top three teams in terms of qualifications to the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_Tournament_at_the_Summer_Olympics" class="mw-redirect" title="Basketball Tournament at the Summer Olympics">Basketball Tournament at the Summer Olympics</a>. Other major international events held in Australia include the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Open" title="Australian Open">Australian Open</a> tennis <a href="/wiki/Grand_Slam_(tennis)" title="Grand Slam (tennis)">grand slam</a> tournament, international cricket matches, and the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Grand_Prix" title="Australian Grand Prix">Australian Formula One Grand Prix</a>. The highest-rating television programs include sports telecasts such as the Summer Olympics, FIFA World Cup, <a href="/wiki/The_Ashes" title="The Ashes">The Ashes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_State_of_Origin" class="mw-redirect" title="Rugby League State of Origin">Rugby League State of Origin</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_final" title="Grand final">grand finals</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">Australian Football League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">[402]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Skiing_in_Australia" title="Skiing in Australia">Skiing in Australia</a> began in the 1860s and snow sports take place in the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Alps" title="Australian Alps">Australian Alps</a> and parts of Tasmania.<sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">[403]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-anthem_explanation-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-anthem_explanation_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Australia's <a href="/wiki/Honors_music" title="Honors music">royal anthem</a> is "<a href="/wiki/God_Save_the_Queen" title="God Save the Queen">God Save the Queen</a>", played in the presence of a member of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Windsor" title="House of Windsor">Royal family</a> when they are in Australia. In other contexts, the <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> of Australia, "<a href="/wiki/Advance_Australia_Fair" title="Advance Australia Fair">Advance Australia Fair</a>", is played.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-languages-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-languages_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">English does not have <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> status.<sup id="cite_ref-language_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-language-3">[2]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-6">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Religion was an optional question on the Census, so percentages for individual religions do not add up to 100%<sup id="cite_ref-statcan1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statcan1-5">[3]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-time-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-time_15-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-time_15-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">There are minor variations from three basic time zones; see <a href="/wiki/Time_in_Australia" title="Time in Australia">Time in Australia</a>.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The earliest recorded use of the word <i>Australia</i> in English was in 1625 in "A note of Australia del Espíritu Santo, written by Sir <a href="/wiki/Richard_Hakluyt" title="Richard Hakluyt">Richard Hakluyt</a>", published by <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Purchas" title="Samuel Purchas">Samuel Purchas</a> in <i>Hakluytus Posthumus</i>, a corruption of the original Spanish name "Austrialia del Espíritu Santo" (Southern Land of the Holy Spirit)<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[36]</a></sup> for an island in <a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[37]</a></sup> The Dutch adjectival form <i>australische</i> was used in a Dutch book in <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jakarta" title="History of Jakarta">Batavia</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>) in 1638, to refer to the newly discovered lands to the south.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[38]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-44"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-44">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">For instance, the 1814 work <i><a href="/wiki/A_Voyage_to_Terra_Australis" title="A Voyage to Terra Australis">A Voyage to Terra Australis</a></i></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-Southern_Ocean-123"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Southern_Ocean_123-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Australia describes the body of water south of its mainland as the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ocean" title="Southern Ocean">Southern Ocean</a>, rather than the Indian Ocean as defined by the <a href="/wiki/International_Hydrographic_Organization" title="International Hydrographic Organization">International Hydrographic Organization</a> (IHO). In 2000, a vote of IHO member nations defined the term "Southern Ocean" as applying only to the waters between <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> and <a href="/wiki/60th_parallel_south" title="60th parallel south">60° south</a> latitude.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[116]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-290"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-290">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In accordance with the Australian Bureau of Statistics source, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mainland_China" title="Mainland China">Mainland China</a> and the Special Administrative Regions of <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> are listed separately</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-295"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-295">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As a percentage of 21,769,209 persons who nominated their ancestry at the 2016 census. The <a href="/wiki/Census_in_Australia" title="Census in Australia">Australian Census</a> collects information on ancestry, but not on race or ethnicity.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-299"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-299">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Australian Bureau of Statistics has stated that most who nominate "Australian" as their ancestry are part of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Celtic_Australian" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Celtic Australian">Anglo-Celtic</a> group.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[289]</a></sup></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-300"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-300">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Of any ancestry. Includes those identifying as <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">Aboriginal Australians</a> or <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait_Islanders" title="Torres Strait Islanders">Torres Strait Islanders</a>. Indigenous identification is separate to the ancestry question on the Australian Census and persons identifying as Aboriginal or Torres Strait Islander may identify any ancestry.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-301"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-301">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Includes those identifying as <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_Australians" title="Aboriginal Australians">Aboriginal Australians</a> or <a href="/wiki/Torres_Strait_Islanders" title="Torres Strait Islanders">Torres Strait Islanders</a>. Indigenous identification is separate to the ancestry question on the Australian Census and persons identifying as Aboriginal or Torres Strait Islander may identify any ancestry.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
